<a href="file.pdf" download>Download PDF</a>

<a href="https://example.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Visit Site</a>

<a href="/doc.txt" download="instructions.txt">Get Instructions</a> ^ZT0LnOhJ

Element: <a>

href (required for linking)

target (optional)

rel (optional)

download (optional) ^vlt0tXjr

Omitting rel="noopener" when using target="_blank", which exposes security risks.

Using download with cross-origin links without proper CORS, which disables the download.

Applying download to non-downloadable resources like dynamic scripts or interactive web apps. ^MKBXUiec

target="_blank" opens a new tab; combining it with rel="noopener" is necessary to prevent access to window.opener for security.

The download attribute only works for same-origin URLs or if the CORS headers allow it. ^M2bjc8P7

The <a> (anchor) element in HTML defines a hyperlink, which is used to navigate to other resources. 

Its behavior and function are determined primarily by the href, target, rel, and download attributes:

href specifies the URL of the resource being linked. It is required for the element to function as a navigational link.

target defines where the linked document will open. Common values include _self (default, same tab), _blank (new tab), _parent, and _top.

rel specifies the relationship between the current document and the linked one. It is important for SEO and security. Common values include noopener, noreferrer, and nofollow, especially in combination with target="_blank" to prevent access to the originating window.

download transforms the hyperlink into a download action. When present, it instructs the browser to download the resource rather than navigating to it, optionally allowing the file to be saved with a specified filename.

When used together, these attributes control the navigation destination, relationship context, and behavior of resource interaction, enhancing both user experience and security.
